Homomorphic Encryption
2/29/24, 9:30 PM - Muhammad Omar Farooq: Based on the given options and considering research-based approaches for improving encryption techniques, you should consider **Homomorphic Encryption**.

Homomorphic encryption allows computations to be performed on encrypted data without decrypting it first. This property is highly desirable for privacy-preserving computation on sensitive data, making it a valuable tool for secure data processing, especially in scenarios where data privacy is paramount.

Homomorphic encryption has seen significant advancements in recent years, with ongoing research aimed at improving its efficiency, security, and applicability in various domains including cloud computing, healthcare, finance, and more.

Therefore, choosing homomorphic encryption can offer enhanced security and privacy guarantees for your encrypted data, along with the ability to perform computations on encrypted data directly, which can be beneficial in various applications.

3/7/24, 1:44 AM - Muhammad Omar Farooq: Here's the classification of each cipher:

1. **DES**
   - Symmetrical
   - Block
   - Substitute

2. **AES**
   - Symmetrical
   - Block
   - Substitute

3. **Rail Fence Cipher**
   - Symmetrical
   - Transposition

4. **Row/Column Cipher**
   - Symmetrical
   - Transposition

5. **Hill Cipher**
   - Symmetrical
   - Product

6. **One-time pad**
   - Symmetrical
   - Stream

7. **Vigenère Cipher**
   - Symmetrical
   - Product

8. **Vernam Cipher**
   - Symmetrical
   - Stream

9. **Autokey Cipher**
   - Symmetrical
   - Stream

10. **Monoalphabetic Cipher**
    - Symmetrical
    - Substitute

11. **Caesar Cipher**
    - Symmetrical
    - Substitute

12. **Shift Cipher**
    - Symmetrical
    - Substitute

13. **Playfair Cipher**
    - Symmetrical
    - Substitute
    - Product

These classifications are based on common properties and characteristics of each cipher. Keep in mind that some ciphers may have characteristics that could fit multiple categories.
3/7/24, 1:45 AM - Muhammad Omar Farooq: Certainly! Here are the strengths and weaknesses of each cipher briefly:

1. **DES (Data Encryption Standard)**
   - Strengths:
     - Well-studied and widely implemented.
     - Resistance against known attacks when used with proper key management.
     - Established and trusted encryption standard for many years.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Relatively small key size (56 bits) by modern standards.
     - Vulnerable to brute-force attacks due to small key space.
     - Slower compared to modern encryption algorithms.

2. **AES (Advanced Encryption Standard)**
   - Strengths:
     - Strong security with key sizes of 128, 192, or 256 bits.
     - Widely adopted and trusted, with efficient implementations.
     - Resistant to known attacks when used correctly with appropriate key sizes.
   - Weaknesses:
     - None known if used correctly with strong key management and implementation.

3. **Rail Fence Cipher**
   - Strengths:
     - Easy to understand and implement, suitable for educational purposes.
     - Provides basic security against casual attackers.
     - Can be used for steganography due to its simplicity.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Vulnerable to frequency analysis, especially with longer messages.
     - Limited security against modern cryptanalysis techniques.
     - Relatively weak encryption compared to more advanced ciphers.

4. **Row/Column Cipher**
   - Strengths:
     - Simple and straightforward to implement.
     - Provides basic security against casual attackers.
     - Can be applied to various data types beyond text.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Vulnerable to frequency analysis, especially with longer messages.
     - Limited security against modern cryptanalysis techniques.
     - Relatively weak encryption compared to more advanced ciphers.

5. **Hill Cipher**
   - Strengths:
     - Provides strong encryption when used with large key matrices.
     - Resistant to frequency analysis due to its mathematical structure.
     - Offers good security when the key is kept secret and secure.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Requires invertible key matrices, which can be challenging to generate.
     - Vulnerable to known-plaintext attacks when the key is short.
     - Inefficient for encryption of large data sets due to computational complexity.

6. **One-time Pad**
   - Strengths:
     - Provides perfect secrecy when used correctly with truly random keys.
     - Resistant to all known attacks, including brute-force and cryptanalysis.
     - Can be used for secure communications in theory if key distribution is feasible.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Requires a key that is as long as the plaintext, making it impractical for most real-world scenarios.
     - Key distribution is challenging, especially for large keys.
     - Reusing keys or any deviation from perfect randomness compromises security.

7. **Vigenère Cipher**
   - Strengths:
     - Provides reasonable security against casual attackers.
     - Relatively easy to understand and implement.
     - More resistant to frequency analysis compared to monoalphabetic ciphers.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Vulnerable to Kasiski examination and other known-plaintext attacks.
     - Susceptible to statistical attacks, especially with long messages.
     - Key management can be challenging, especially for long and random keys.

8. **Vernam Cipher**
   - Strengths:
     - Provably secure if used with truly random keys of the same length as the plaintext.
     - Provides perfect secrecy when used correctly.
     - Simple and straightforward to implement.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Requires a key that is as long as the plaintext, limiting practical use.
     - Key distribution is challenging, especially for large keys.
     - Reusing keys or any deviation from perfect randomness compromises security.

9. **Autokey Cipher**
   - Strengths:
     - Provides additional security compared to simple Vigenère cipher.
     - Resistant to Kasiski examination and other known-plaintext attacks.
     - Offers better security than traditional Vigenère with shorter keys.
   - Weaknesses:
     - Vulnerable to known-plaintext attacks, especially when the key is short.
     - Key management can be challenging, especially for long and random keys.
     - Reusing keys or any deviation from perfect randomness compromises security.

10. **Monoalphabetic Cipher**
    - Strengths:
      - Simple to understand and implement.
      - Useful for educational purposes to introduce basic concepts of cryptography.
      - Can provide basic security for low-security applications when combined with strong key management.
    - Weaknesses:
      - Vulnerable to frequency analysis, especially with larger messages.
      - Provides weak security against modern cryptanalysis techniques.
      - Each letter in the plaintext is always encrypted to the same letter in the ciphertext, making it susceptible to pattern analysis.

11. **Caesar Cipher**
    - Strengths:
      - Simple and easy to understand.
      - Useful for educational purposes to introduce basic concepts of cryptography.
      - Provides basic security against casual attackers.
    - Weaknesses:
      - Vulnerable to brute-force attacks, as there are only 25 possible keys.
      - Provides weak security against modern cryptanalysis techniques.
      - Each letter in the plaintext is always encrypted to the same letter in the ciphertext, making it susceptible to frequency analysis.

12. **Shift Cipher**
    - Strengths:
      - Simple and easy to understand.
      - Useful for educational purposes to introduce basic concepts of cryptography.
      - Provides basic security against casual attackers.
    - Weaknesses:
      - Vulnerable to brute-force attacks, as there are only 25 possible keys.
      - Provides weak security against modern cryptanalysis techniques.
      - Each letter in the plaintext is always encrypted to the same letter in the ciphertext, making it susceptible to frequency analysis.

13. **Playfair Cipher**
    - Strengths:
      - Provides reasonable security against basic cryptanalysis techniques.
      - Relatively easy to implement and use.
      - Preserves the frequency distribution of plaintext letters, making it resistant to certain frequency analysis attacks.
    - Weaknesses:
      - Vulnerable to known-plaintext attacks, especially when the key is short or weak.
      - Key management can be challenging, especially for long and random keys.
      - Requires careful handling of repeated letters in the plaintext, as it can affect the encryption process.

3/19/24, 11:56 AM - Muhammad Omar Farooq: INTERACTIVE SESSION BLUES Nels sas 
Monitoring Employees on Networks: Unethical or Good Business? 
The Internet has become an extremely valuable 
business tool, but it’s also a huge distraction for 
workers on the job. Employees are wasting valuable 
company time by surfing inappropriate websites 
(Facebook, shopping, sports, etc.), sending and re- 
ceiving personal email, texting to friends, and down- 
loading videos and music. According to a survey by 
International Data Corp (IDC), 30 to 40 percent of 
Internet access is spent on non-work-related brows- 
ing, and a staggering 60 percent of all online pur- 
chases are made during working hours. UK-based 
employment site MyJobGroup.co.uk surveyed 1,000 
British workers and found that almost 6 percent of 
them spent over an hour a day using social media of 
some kind, including Facebook. This is roughly one- 
eighth of their workday. By extension, about 2 mil- 
lion of Britain’s 34-million-person workforce likely 
were doing the same, costing the British economy 
about 14 billion pounds in lost productivity. 
Many companies have begun monitoring em- 
ployee use of email and the Internet, sometimes 
without their knowledge. Many tools are now avail- 
able for this purpose from vendors such as Veriato 
OsMonitor, Work Examiner, Mobistealth, and 
Spytech. These products enable companies to record 
online searches, monitor file downloads and uploads, 
record keystrokes, keep tabs on emails, create tran- 
scripts of chats, or take certain screenshots of images 
displayed on computer screens. Instant messaging, 
text messaging, and social media monitoring are also 
increasing. 
Microsoft Corporation collects and analyzes data 
on the frequency of chats, emails, and meetings be- 
tween its staff and clients using its own Office 365 
services to measure employee productivity, manage- 
ment effectiveness, and work-life balance. Tracking 
email, chats, and calendar appointments can show 
how employees spend an average of 20 hours of their 
work time each week. The company only allows 
managers to look at groups of five or more workers. 
Microsoft sales team members have received per- 
sonalized dashboards that show how they spend their 
time, but this information is shielded from managers. 
The dashboards offers recommendations on how to 
build out networks of contacts and spend more time 
with customers rather than in internal meetings. 
Microsoft also sells workplace analytics software 
to 
other companies, such as Macy’s Inc., which ana- 
lyzed data on staff work-life balance by measuring 
how many hours employees spent sending emails 
and logged in online outside of business hours. 
Mortgage giant Freddie Mac used Microsoft's tools 
to 
gauge how much time workers spent in meetings 
and try to determine whether some of those gather- 
ings were redundant. 
Although U.S. companies have the legal right to 
monitor employee Internet and email activity while 
they are at work, is such monitoring unethical, or 
is 
it 
simply good business? Managers worry about 
the loss of time and employee productivity when 
employees are focusing on personal rather than com- 
pany business. Too much time on personal business 
translates into lost revenue. Some employees may 
even be billing time they spend pursuing personal 
interests online to clients, thus overcharging them. 
If personal traffic on company networks is too 
high, it can also clog the company’s network so that 
legitimate business work cannot be performed. GMI 
Insurance Services, which serves the U.S. transporta- 
tion industry, found that employees were download- 
ing a great deal of music and streaming video and 
storing the files on company servers. GMI's server 
backup space was being eaten up. 
When employees use email or the web (includ- 
ing social networks) at employer facilities or with 
employer equipment, anything they do, includ- 
ing anything illegal, carries the company’s name. 
Therefore, the employer can be traced and held liable. 
Management in many firms fear that racist, sexually 
explicit, or other potentially offensive material ac- 
cessed or traded by their employees could result in 
adverse publicity and even lawsuits for the firm. Even 
if the company is found not to be liable, responding 
to 
lawsuits could run up huge legal bills. Companies 
also fear leakage of confidential information and trade 
secrets through email or social networks. U.S. compa- 
nies have the legal right to monitor what employees 
are 
doing with company equipment during business 
hours. The question is whether electronic surveillance 
is 
an appropriate tool for maintaining an efficient and 
positive workplace. Some companies try to ban all per- 
sonal activities on corporate networks—zero tolerance.
Chapter 7 Telecommunications, the Internet, and Wireless Technology 
Others block employee access to specific websites or 
social sites, closely monitor email messages, or limit 
personal time on the web. 
Should all employees be monitored while work- 
ing? Not necessarily. Not every workforce, workplace, 
or work culture and environment is a candidate for 
electronic surveillance. The decision depends on the 
company and the work environment an employer 
wants to create. A major concern of some employers 
is 
the potential damage to a work culture that fos- 
ters trust, employee commitment, and motivation. 
Electronic surveillance of employees could prove 
highly counterproductive in such an environment. 
No solution is problem-free, but many consultants 
believe companies should write corporate policies on 
employee email, social media, and Internet use. Many 
workers are unaware that employers have the right 
should include explicit ground rules that state, by posi- 
tion or level, under what circumstances employees can 
use company facilities for email, blogging, or web surf- 
ing. The policies should also inform employees whether 
these activities are monitored and explain why. 
The rules should be tailored to specific business 
needs and organizational cultures. For example, in- 
vestment firms will need to allow many of their em- 
ployees access to other investment sites. A company 
dependent on widespread information sharing, inno- 
vation, and independence could very well find that 
monitoring creates more problems than it solves.

Ways Your Boss Is Spying on You,” Wall Street Journal, July 19, 2019;

monitor and collect data about them. The policies

and

November 25, 2019.

Question 1: What is the main objective of the SUNRISE project?
Stepwise solution: The main objective of the SUNRISE project is to accelerate and facilitate the integration of photovoltaic systems in buildings and the electricity network to reduce the cost of photovoltaic systems and become competitive with conventional energy production in the future liberalised energy market.
Question 2: What are the barriers that need to be addressed in order to achieve the project's objective?
Stepwise solution: The identified barriers include administrative, market, technological, and perception barriers.
Question 3: How will the project address the identified barriers?
Stepwise solution: The project will work on initiating a dialogue between the photovoltaic industry and utilities to find a balance between centralised and decentralised electricity generation, keeping in mind grid stability and system control. Additionally, the project will collaborate with relevant stakeholders such as architects, electrical installers, and European utilities to facilitate the integration of photovoltaic systems in buildings.
Question 4: What is the role of standards in the project?
Stepwise solution: Standards play an important role in the project as they can contribute to harmonisation and simplification of processes, leading to reduced costs. The project will work on developing new products and awareness-raising, and will communicate proposals to national and international standardisation committees.
Question 5: How long will the project last?
Stepwise solution: The project started on 1 May 2007 and will last for 30 months until 1 November 2009.
Question 6: What is the consortium comprised of?
Stepwise solution: The SUNRISE project is being carried out by a consortium of five partners, which represent the photovoltaic industry, construction sector, architects, and electrical installers. Electricité de France (EDF) has also been subcontracted to facilitate the dialogue with European utilities.
Question 7: What is the project's coordination?
Stepwise solution: The project is coordinated by the European Photovoltaic Industry Association (EPIA) with the support of Wirtschaft und Infrastruktur GmbH & Co Planungs KG.
everybody loves raymond - Season 1-5
Everybody Loves Raymond is an American sitcom that originally aired on CBS from 1996 to 2007. The show was created by Phil Rosenthal, who also served as an executive producer. It stars Ray Romano as the titular character, Raymond Barone, a successful sports writer living in Long Island with his wife Debra (Patricia Heaton) and their three children. The show follows the daily life of the Barone family, including Raymond's relationships with his wife, parents, and siblings.
The first season of Everybody Loves Raymond premiered on September 19, 1996, and ran for 23 episodes until May 20, 1997. The show was well-received by critics and audiences alike, with the season finale earning a 24.5 million viewers. The show continued to gain popularity throughout its run, with the fifth season premiering on September 18, 2000, and running for 26 episodes until May 15, 2001.
Everybody Loves Raymond was praised for its witty writing, well-developed characters, and strong performances from the cast. The show won several awards during its run, including multiple Emmy Awards, Golden Globe Awards, and Screen Actors Guild Awards. It is widely regarded as one of the greatest sitcoms of all time, and continues to be syndicated around the world.

Blog Tour: The Lost Ones by Sheba Karim
Title: The Lost Ones
Author: Sheba Karim
Publication Date: October 17, 2019
Publisher: Simon Pulse
Genre: Young Adult, Fantasy
Pages: 368

Summary:
A magical and heartwarming tale of love, loss, and the power of family from debut author Sheba Karim.
Nisha was only seven when her parents died in a car accident, but their memory lives on through the stories she tells herself and her five-year-old brother, Amir. The two of them have been inseparable since, but now Nisha is thirteen, and Amir is growing up fast. When Nisha starts to realize that she can’t protect him forever, she becomes determined to find a way to bring their parents back—or at least find a way to keep her brother safe without her.
She sets off on a quest to find the Lost Ones, a mystical group of people who might be able to help her. Along the way, she meets new friends and allies, including a boy named Sabeen who has lost his own parents in a similar tragedy. Together, they face challenges that test their courage and resilience, but also learn the true meaning of family, love, and hope.
Review:
The Lost Ones is a beautifully written story about grief, loss, and the power of love. Sheba Karim’s writing is poignant and heartwarming, and she tackles some heavy themes with sensitivity and grace. The characters are well-developed and relatable, especially Nisha and Amir, who are both struggling to cope with their loss in different ways.
The plot is engaging and suspenseful, with plenty of twists and turns to keep readers on the edge of their seats. The magical elements are skillfully woven throughout the story, adding an extra layer of depth and wonder to the narrative.
One of the things that struck me most about this book was the way it tackles grief and loss in a realistic and nuanced way. Karim doesn’t shy away from the difficult emotions and situations that come with losing someone you love, but she also offers hope and comfort through the power of family and friendship.
The Lost Ones is a moving and uplifting story that will resonate with readers of all ages. It’s a beautiful tribute to the bonds of love and family, and a reminder that even in the darkest times, there is always hope for healing and growth.

вересня 2019 року вийшла книга "The Lost Ones" від Sheba Karim. Книжка належить до жанру молодіжної фентезі та має 368 сторінок.
У цій історії розповідається про дівчину на ім'я Ніша, яка зневажає втрату своїх батьків у автокатастрофі, коли їй за 13 років. Вона змушена прийняти виклики та випробування, що починаються від її найближчих, але також і від незнайомих людей.
Ніша намагається знайти шлях до спасіння свого брата Аміра, який є єдиним джерелом щастя для неї. Вона починає шукати "Втрачені", групу людей, які можуть допомогти їй забезпечити безпеку свого брата.
У процесі пошуків, Нія знайомиться з хлопцем на ім'я Саббен, який теж втратив своїх батьків. Разом вони проходять через безліч випробувань і стикаються зі злом, яке охороняє їхні батьки.
"The Lost Ones" - це історія про любов, втрату та надії. Sheba Karim розповідає про те, як любов до близьких може допомогти пережити найсмертельніші випробування, і що є більш важливим - любов або втрата?

4/25/24, 10:23 AM - Umair 20CP UET: Title: Installation and Configuration of Monitorix on CentOS 7

Executive Summary:
This report outlines the steps taken to install and configure Monitorix, a system monitoring tool, on CentOS 7. Monitorix provides a comprehensive platform for monitoring system resources, services, and network interfaces, enabling efficient system administration and troubleshooting. This report covers the installation, configuration, and key features of Monitorix, making it an ideal guide for system administrators and IT professionals.

Introduction:
Monitorix is a free, open-source system monitoring tool designed for Linux systems. It offers a web-based interface for monitoring system resources, services, and network interfaces, making it an ideal choice for CentOS 7. Monitorix supports various plugins, allowing for extended monitoring capabilities, including:

- System resources (CPU, memory, disk usage, and network interfaces)
- Services (HTTP, FTP, SSH, and more)
- Network interfaces (traffic and error monitoring)
- Customizable dashboards and graphs

Installation:

1. Update the package list: `sudo yum update -y`
2. Install epel-release: `sudo yum install epel-release -y`
3. Install Monitorix: `sudo yum install monitorix -y`

Configuration:

1. Edit the Monitorix configuration file: `sudo nano /etc/monitorix/monitorix.conf`
2. Set the web interface settings:
    - `enabled = yes`
    - `host = 0.0.0.0` (allow access from any IP)
    - `port = 8080` (default port)
3. Configure email notifications (optional):
    - `mail_server = <mail_server_IP>`
    - `mail_user = <mail_username>`
    - `mail_pass = <mail_password>`
4. Restart the Monitorix service: `sudo systemctl restart monitorix`

Accessing Monitorix:

1. Open a web browser and navigate to `http://<IP_Address>:8080` (replace <IP_Address> with the server's IP address)
2. Log in with the default credentials (username: `admin`, password: `monitorix`)

Key Features:

- System Resources:
    - CPU usage and temperature monitoring
    - Memory usage and swap space monitoring
    - Disk usage and I/O monitoring
    - Network interface traffic and error monitoring
- Services:
    - Monitoring of system services, including HTTP, FTP, and SSH
    - Customizable service monitoring and alerting
- Network Interfaces:
    - Monitoring of network interface traffic and errors
    - Customizable network interface monitoring and alerting
- Customizable Dashboards and Graphs:
    - Create custom dashboards for specific monitoring needs
    - Customize graph colors, labels, and settings

Conclusion:
Monitorix has been successfully installed and configured on CentOS 7, providing a comprehensive platform for system monitoring and administration. Its web-based interface and customizable dashboards make it an ideal tool for system administrators and IT professionals. Regular updates and maintenance will ensure optimal performance and security.

Recommendations:

- Regularly update Monitorix to ensure the latest features and security patches
- Customize the dashboard to suit specific monitoring needs
- Integrate Monitorix with other system administration tools for enhanced monitoring and troubleshooting capabilities
- Explore additional plugins and features to extend monitoring capabilities

Note: This report assumes a basic understanding of Linux and system administration concepts. The installation and configuration steps may vary depending on the specific environment and requirements.
